<div id="review_79912243" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/79912243" />
    <a title="Lauren" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1676535-lauren"><img alt="Lauren" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499022950p2/1676535.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/79912243?book_show_action=true">Dec 04, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lauren" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lauren" href="/user/show/1676535-lauren">Lauren</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1676535-lauren?shelf=own">own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer79912243" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3017131783217907064">After reading Rachel Ward's Numbers last year, I was eager to read more by her, especially since her future books' would be part of the same world. Sadly enough, while The Chaos is, without a doubt, an interesting and suspenseful addition, it truly didn't live up to Numbers, in my opinion. <br/><br/>The Chaos begins the story of Adam, the child of Jem and Spider- the main characters of Numbers. Just like his beloved mother, Adam can see the people's death dates as well as what will happen to them when he </span>
  <span id="freeText3017131783217907064" style="display:none">After reading Rachel Ward's Numbers last year, I was eager to read more by her, especially since her future books' would be part of the same world. Sadly enough, while The Chaos is, without a doubt, an interesting and suspenseful addition, it truly didn't live up to Numbers, in my opinion. <br /><br />The Chaos begins the story of Adam, the child of Jem and Spider- the main characters of Numbers. Just like his beloved mother, Adam can see the people's death dates as well as what will happen to them when he looks into their eyes. In his opinion, this is not the best ability, as not only was he able to predict his mother's death, but he has also become emotionally scarred by everyone else's as well. After a few incidents, Jem begins to learn it's best to stay under the radar, though everything changes when he realizes how people's numbers are in January 2027. Knowing that nothing good is to come from this, he teams up with Sarah, another teen with a harrowing past of her own, to stop this. However, will they be able to in time? More importantly, will they come out alive? Only time and more pages will tell in this fast-paced thriller.<br /><br />One of my favorite parts of Numbers was the characters, Jem and Spider specifically, but in The Chaos I had the hardest of times relating to Adam and Sarah. Sure, I found them and their stories interesting, but when it down to it I didn't really have much in common with them; ultimately bring this story down a few notches.<br /><br />Thankfully, the plot was what saved this novel, because not only did I love the premise, but the execution was also great. There wasn't a moment where I wasn't contemplating what would happen next: Would Sarah and Jem come out alive? What was going to happen in January 2027? There were so many questions, making this novel one I ripped through quickly as possible. <br /><br />Rachel's writing has also improved, as she did a great job of switching narrators in a way that created lots of tension and suspense and had plenty of decent world building. However, I will admit, I didn't find the ending she gave to be the greatest. I was left with plenty of questions, but with the promise of a sequel in the future, I'm sure they'll be answered then. <br /><br />While The Chaos wasn't my favorite book of Rachel's so far, I did still find it to be an enjoyable read overall. I will definitely be reading the conclusion to the trilogy, coming out next year. So, in all, I suggest this read to teens of all ages as well as adult fans of YA.<br /><br />Grade: B</span>
  <a data-text-id="3017131783217907064" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

I just loved Nan. :( <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> But I think Ward is an engaging, talented, emotionally-affective writer and I look forward to reentering the world she's created anyways.<br /></span>

<div id="review_459539036" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cam T" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cam T" href="/user/show/13933508-cam-t">Cam T</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer11917596710375551275">I would recommend the book The Chaos by Rachel Ward to a friend because of it’s rich plot, suspense, and variety of conflicts. Throughout The Chaos there are multiple conflicts. One is the overall conflict; the one Adam can see coming on the date of 01012027. He knows it will strike London so he decides to warn people of the upcoming danger. “The first of January. Save yourselves, your families! Get out of London!”(Pg. 250) Hoping to help people, Adam is arrested for breaking a law in the terror</span>
  <span id="freeText11917596710375551275" style="display:none">I would recommend the book The Chaos by Rachel Ward to a friend because of it’s rich plot, suspense, and variety of conflicts. Throughout The Chaos there are multiple conflicts. One is the overall conflict; the one Adam can see coming on the date of 01012027. He knows it will strike London so he decides to warn people of the upcoming danger. “The first of January. Save yourselves, your families! Get out of London!”(Pg. 250) Hoping to help people, Adam is arrested for breaking a law in the terrorism act of 2018. He is accused of murder and creating conspiracies to spread terror. He is then thrown into jail one day before the chaos will hit. Meanwhile, his friend Sarah, is facing another struggle. After having her newborn baby Mia treated at a local hospital, children’s protection services visit her at a friends house where she is staying. They soon find out the friend is on drugs and, even though Sarah is not using them, they take Mia. “She’s gone. They took Mia, she’s gone.”(Pg. 239) <br /><br />	Another reason I would recommend this book to a firend is because of the plot twist in the end of the story. Even Information from Book 1 leads you on to believe on event. “Why? Why did she die Sarah? Why did her number change?”(Pg. 335) Suspense is a tool the author uses quite frequently and effectively, and my third reason for this book’s recommendation. A good example of when the author uses suspense is when Sarah falls asleep and Adam investigates the crying upstairs. “The baby’s face is red from crying, her eyelashes wet from tears…she opens her eyes. I gasp. No. Oh god please, no. Like a bullet to my brain, her number shoots through me. 01012027.”(Pg. 162) <br /><br />	Some readers may think there is too much violence in this story. It is a strong argument, but ask yourself, is it really the same story without it. The whole story revolves around catastrophe, death, that is what the numbers represent.ss As you can see, there are many reasons why I chose to recommend The Chaos to a friend. It is a brilliant read and I’m positive that any suspense and action loving reader would think the same about this amazing book.<br /></span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8036025199876397134">Numbers 2: The Chaos by Rachel Ward <br/><br/>After I finished “Numbers 2” by Rachel Ward, my mind was a complete mess. I like how a lot of things are happening at the same time, but sometimes it’s hard to wrap my mind on what is going on. <br/><br/>The tone and plot of the story let the readers know that there is a lot going on in this story. Numbers 2 by Rachel Ward has a way of describing the real world society, the side where it’s messed up. This makes me think because not a lot of people has encountered this “</span>
  <span id="freeText8036025199876397134" style="display:none">Numbers 2: The Chaos by Rachel Ward <br /><br />After I finished “Numbers 2” by Rachel Ward, my mind was a complete mess. I like how a lot of things are happening at the same time, but sometimes it’s hard to wrap my mind on what is going on. <br /><br />The tone and plot of the story let the readers know that there is a lot going on in this story. Numbers 2 by Rachel Ward has a way of describing the real world society, the side where it’s messed up. This makes me think because not a lot of people has encountered this “dark” side of the society. This book is based on two different people’s perspective, and how they are destined to have a connection with one another, in a kind of disturbing way. Since it’s two peoples lives, more events happen, and sometimes they happen at the same time. The result of this is, before I am even done comprehending what happened and how I feel about it, another event happens and I would have to deal with a lot of events at the same time. The author also vividly describes what is going on in the character’s head, which puts even more on what I’m thinking when I read.<br /><br />There are 2 main characters in this book; Adam and Sarah. Both have extremely realistic attitudes and mind flow. Characterization is one of the many areas where Rachel Ward excels at. <br /><br />In my opinion, the plot moves kind of sluggish and slow at the beginning, but really picks itself up later on in the book. <br /><br />All in all, I really enjoyed reading “Numbers 2”. I have never been so overwhelmed by the characters’ feelings and the complicated events before; and I think that is exactly what Rachel Ward wanted to us to feel when we read this messy yet cliff hanging book.<br /></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/327471-kristen?shelf=paranormal-fantasy">paranormal-fantasy</a>,

<span id="freeTextContainer412418501105151284">Why I read this: I read the first book and figured that I'd give the second book a chance.<br/><br/>Plot: Adam is the son of Jem, a young woman who we met in the first novel Numbers. He must figure out what is going to happen in January of 2027 since that is the deathdate he sees over many of the people living in London.<br/><br/>Sarah has been dreaming about Adam since her father got her pregnant. In her dream, Adam steals her baby away and jumps through a fire. When she meets him in the flesh, she panics. Why has</span>
  <span id="freeText412418501105151284" style="display:none">Why I read this: I read the first book and figured that I'd give the second book a chance.<br /><br />Plot: Adam is the son of Jem, a young woman who we met in the first novel Numbers. He must figure out what is going to happen in January of 2027 since that is the deathdate he sees over many of the people living in London.<br /><br />Sarah has been dreaming about Adam since her father got her pregnant. In her dream, Adam steals her baby away and jumps through a fire. When she meets him in the flesh, she panics. Why has this evil young man come to life, why is he here? And why is she so drawn to him?<br /><br />A book that is full of suspense, action and some terrifying events that really blew me away. I enjoyed the first book, but it felt slow and this book was so involved and had so much going on, I could barely put it down. Definitely a fantastic sequel.<br /><br />Characters: I really liked the characters. They're not perfect, not in the least. They're a little bit crazy in their own ways. Adam sometimes loses control of himself and he at one point has to run away from hurting his own Nan. Sarah has a troubled past, her father having raped her since the age of 12. She finds more and more trouble as she tries to save her baby from Him, her father - who she is deathly afraid of and also from this new threat of a boy from her dreams who takes her darling girl away from her.<br /><br />Relatability: Definitely a great novel for those that like suspense.<br /><br />Cover Commentary: Lovely. I like the theme of these covers that so match the books.</span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_177098107" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/177098107" />
    <a title="Mateja" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2655289-mateja"><img alt="Mateja" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546419254p2/2655289.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/177098107?book_show_action=true">Jun 16, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mateja" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mateja" href="/user/show/2655289-mateja">Mateja</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer177098107" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7741519734659931468">Just like the first book in the series Chaos left me with a myriad of emotions. The storyline I absolutely loved, the characters not so much. <br/><br/>The plot was thrilling, chilling and often downright terrifying. Rachel Ward pulls no punches and spares us readers nothing. The storytelling in honest, blunt, straightforward and doesn’t shy away from the dangerous scenes described in a gritty detail that makes you cringe. There’s not a dull moment in this book and often you’ll feel the need to put the bo</span>
  <span id="freeText7741519734659931468" style="display:none">Just like the first book in the series Chaos left me with a myriad of emotions. The storyline I absolutely loved, the characters not so much. <br /><br />The plot was thrilling, chilling and often downright terrifying. Rachel Ward pulls no punches and spares us readers nothing. The storytelling in honest, blunt, straightforward and doesn’t shy away from the dangerous scenes described in a gritty detail that makes you cringe. There’s not a dull moment in this book and often you’ll feel the need to put the book down for a moment to rest, but at the same time you won’t be able to, as the story pulls you in completely. <br /><br />I started off liking Adam and Mia. Life has clearly dealt them some hard choices and it wasn’t hard to feel bad for them. But as the story progressed and the situation became more difficult I felt like often they made it so on their own. When something could be resolved with calm or easier to get people to listen by approaching the matter rationally, they acted like, quite frankly, crazy people. The kind you turn away from when they start talking at you and make little sense. <br /><br />And even though at the end they profess their love for each other, the only one who’s feelings were believable was Adam. Sarah was distrustful till the very end and her sudden love profession fell short in the emotional department. <br /><br />I will read the next and last book in the series as I still haven’t gotten an explanation as to what exactly caused the disastrous day in London. Theories were thrown about during the book, but nothing was explained concretely. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7741519734659931468" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_173415700" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/173415700" />
    <a title="Nick" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/724379-nick"><img alt="Nick" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/173415700?book_show_action=true">Jun 03, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nick" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nick" href="/user/show/724379-nick">Nick</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/724379-nick?shelf=young-adult-fiction">young-adult-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer173415700" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4342187227521138501">After reading the first volume of this series, I didn't see how a sequel could possibly work. Luckily, the author proved me wrong. The story isn't so much about the idea of predicting the future as it is about the difficulties in figuring out what to do if you CAN see the future.<br/>For instance, if you were absolutely, positively convinced that something was going to happen three days from now, who could you tell? Who would believe you? And how would you differentiate yourself from the crazies, the</span>
  <span id="freeText4342187227521138501" style="display:none">After reading the first volume of this series, I didn't see how a sequel could possibly work. Luckily, the author proved me wrong. The story isn't so much about the idea of predicting the future as it is about the difficulties in figuring out what to do if you CAN see the future.<br />For instance, if you were absolutely, positively convinced that something was going to happen three days from now, who could you tell? Who would believe you? And how would you differentiate yourself from the crazies, the schemers and every other kind of person who SAYS they can predict the future?<br />Then, there is the "Appointment in Samara" paradox, in which the future you try to prevent is caused by your trying to prevent it. What do you do?<br />The story contained one very odd apparent factual error...the Eurasian tectonic plate's edge is at Iceland, not England [which is why all those volcanoes do not pop up in the British Isles]. A different kind of disaster would work just as well, but the one described is more than a bit difficult to achieve, given that.<br />What still is not addressed, by the end of book 2, is how many other people can see some form of the future. We have three examples so far, with hints that there are more, but how? Why?<br />I look forward to reading the third book, which seems to take the story another generation into the future.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4342187227521138501" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground">Readers also enjoyed</h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent"><div class='bookCarousel'>
<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_307019'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/307019.Friedrich"><img alt="Friedrich" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1347664846l/307019._SY160_.jpg" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('LSTz9zppq3BuHgnt7EKodMJHizY0AqK8LK8DkLObrnlFD3P/HKLKlBIU712QFxtjXMrEZX1TkqZcVsXdRQ5lMQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('wGlxFuSflvtofaAUoVgflVdelh8JcGcEqT09pkQSaE+oQvEewlT3HxR3RqTdDayCydPZTEAhVx7ZxPvrsoejBw==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>
